*****
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
MIKE QUIGLEY, County Commissioner

PROPOSED ORDINAN

~

AMENDMENT

AMENDMENT TO THE COOK COUNTY ETHICS ORDINANCE
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS:
Section 1. Section 2.9 of Article II of the Cook County Ethics Ordinance is hereby amended, and as
amended shall read as follows:

1086

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
2.9

Post Employment Restrictions

(a)

No former official or employee shall assist or represent any person other than the County
in any judicial or administrative proceeding involving the County if the official or
employee was counsel of record or participated personally and substantially in the
proceeding during his or her term of office or employment.

(b)

No former official or employee shall assist or represent any person in any business
transaction involving the County, if the official or employee participated personally and
substantially in that transaction during his or her term of office or employment.

(c)

No former official or employee may, for a period of ene two year~ after the termination
of his or her term of office or employment, knowingly accept employment or receive
compensation or fees for services from an employer if the employee or official, during
the year immediately preceding the termination of County employment and on behalf of
the County participated personally and substantially in the decision to award County
contracts with a cumulative value of over $25,000 to the person or entity, or its parent or
subsidiary.

(d)

The requirements of this Section may be waived by the Board of Ethics if the Board of
Ethics finds in writing that the County's negotiations and decisions regarding the
procurement of the contract or contracts were not materially affected by any potential for
employment of that official or employee by the employer.

(e)

This Section applies only to persons who terminate an affected position on or after the
effective date of this Ordinance.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment be referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 270505). The motion carried
unanimously.
PROPOSED RESOLUTIONS

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
MIKE QUIGLEY, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the 2000 Census determined that minorities account for 52.4 percent of the population of
Cook County; and
WHEREAS, minority-owned businesses with paid employees constitute only 14.5 percent of the total
number of firms, 2.9 percent of total business sales and receipts, 4.8 percent of total employees, and 3.6
percent of total payroll in Cook County, according to the 1997 Economic Census; and
WHEREAS, women-owned businesses with paid employees constitute only 16 percent of the total
number of firms, 4.1 percent of total business sales and receipts, 7.7 percent of total employees, and 5.7
percent of total payroll in Cook County, according to the 1997 Economic Census; and

1087

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
WHEREAS, this dramatic under-representation of minorities and women in the economic life of Cook
County is a serious socioeconomic problem; and
WHEREAS, the certification of women and minority business enterprises was originally established in
order to help women and minority-owned businesses by increasing their opportunities and ending the
disparity in contracts awarded to women and minority owned businesses; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners rightly enacted the Cook County Minority
Business Enterprise/Women's Business Enterprise Ordinance to address the problem of low minority and
women-owned business participation; and
WHEREAS, abuse in the County's minority and women-owned business assistance programs harms
those minority and women-owned businesses which abide by the rules and should be the legitimate
beneficiaries of the Cook County Minority Business Enterprise/Women's Business Enterprise Ordinance;
and
WHEREAS, recently a sub-contract with a county certified minority business was found by a federal
magistrate to serve no "commercially useful" function and has exposed the County to lawsuits; and
WHEREAS, other local government bodies, such as Maricopa County, Arizona, have determined that it
is better to outsource their MBE/WBE certification programs because outsourcing is more cost effective,
non-politicized and objective.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that an outside, independent, audit of all current
MBE/WBE contracts be conducted to determine the legitimacy of their current MBE/WBE status; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County should immediately begin the process of outsourcing
the certification of MBE/WBE contractors through a competitive bid process.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Contract Compliance. (Comm. No. 270506). The motion carried
unanimously.

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, 88,000 parcels (excluding religious exemptions) of all Cook County real estate tax parcels
have been declared tax exempt by Illinois Law; and
WHEREAS, there is no uniform method for reviewing the basis for such tax exemption after it is initially
granted; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Assessor annually reviews the owners' affidavit of exempt property which
states the actual use of the land; and

1088

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

WHEREAS, there should be a more detailed review periodically to protect Cook County taxpayers from
tax exemptions where they are no longer warranted by the manner in which the land is being used.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Assessor shall for all exempt
property at least every five years review the basis for all exemptions granted to real estate property
owners to determine if the basis for the exemption is still in existence; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Assessor shall require every five years any property owner
claiming an exemption to file certified information that proves the continuing basis for an exemption
exists;
AND BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that if the Assessor finds from the evidence presented by the
property owner that the basis for the exemption no longer exists, the Assessor shall return the property to
the tax rolls and the Assessor shall refer the evidence to the Illinois Department of Revenue and the
State's Attorney of Cook County for appropriate action.

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Tax and Revenue Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 270507). The motion carried
unanimously.

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO and PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the County of Cook has been in a budget crisis during its fiscal year 2005; and
WHEREAS, in order to balance the budget, not raise taxes and place further burden on the tax paying
body of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, in order to not experience the same last minute budgetary hardships again in fiscal year
2006 it is important for the Cook County Board of Commissioners to begin thinking about and acting
upon the budgetary processes for the next year in advance; and
WHEREAS, in order to save money for the taxpayers of Cook County and to balance the County's
budget, the County of Cook needs to enter into an intergovernmental relationship and agreement with the
Forest Preserve District of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, by conducting a study to realize the amount of tax dollars that will be saved by researching
the feasibility of consolidating the Finance and Administrative Department functions and the Planning
and Development Department functions both of the Forest Preserve District into the County of Cook; and
WHEREAS, the combined budgets of these two departments within the Forest Preserve District can be
transferred and combined into the one department within the County of Cook.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners, that this text
be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body and this Resolution be referred to the
Finance Committee and the Legislation and Intergovernmental Relations Committee and of the Cook
County Board of Commissioners for further discussion.

1089

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Finance (Comm. No. 270508) and the Committee on Legislation and
Intergovernmental Relations (Comm. No. 270509). The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
MIKE QUIGLEY, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, Cook County, following Section 15-65 of the Property Tax Code of Illinois, exempts all
property from taxes when "actually and exclusively used for charitable or beneficent purposes, and not
leased or other wise used with a view to profit"; and
WHEREAS, not-for-profit hospitals are granted property tax exemptions as a part of this exemption
class; and
WHEREAS, not-for-profit hospitals have a special obligation to the public because they are supported by
the taxpayers and in exchange for their tax-exempt status, not-for-profit hospitals are expected to serve a
charitable mission and put the health needs of the community first; and
WHEREAS, it is important that not-for-profit hospitals that receive public benefits through tax
exemptions should return that benefit to the public through their charity care programs; and
WHEREAS, hospitals throughout Illinois will be filing reports under the Community Benefits Act of
Illinois for the first time this year; and
WHEREAS, these reports will provide information to the public about the hospitals' organizational
mission statements and will disclose the Community Benefits Plans for serving the health care needs of
the community; and
WHEREAS, other counties and government jurisdictions have already had cases that required them to
address how tax exemption status should be determined in relation to not-for-profit hospitals; and
WHEREAS, there are seventy-six hospitals in Cook County, fifty-four of which are non-profit or church
operated; and
WHEREAS, any change to the current tax exemption status would have far reaching affects on the
economic impact hospitals have in Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board, or the appointed committee
thereof, hold a hearing to determine how not-for-profit hospitals' charity care practices should impact
their tax exempt status; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Illinois Attorney General's Office, The Illinois Department of
Revenue and the Cook County Assessor's office should be available to provide information at this
hearing regarding the current status of tax-exemptions for not-for-profit hospitals in Cook County and
Illinois.

1090

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Tax and Revenue Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 270512). The motion carried
unanimously.

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ROBERTO MALDONADO, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, over seventy non-profit hospitals benefit from property tax exemptions in Cook County and
have a moral, financial and legal responsibility to provide quality health care to the poor and uninsured;
and
WHEREAS, in June of 2005, non-profit hospitals will begin filing an annual report known as a
"Community Benefits Plan," in accordance with state law which will include the amount of charity care
and other community benefits the hospital provides; and
WHEREAS, in addition to receiving exemptions from Cook County property taxes (which according to
independent research accounts for approximately 20% of the total annual value of the hospital's
preferential tax status), non-profit hospitals in Cook County also may receive exemptions from various
federal and state income taxes, state and local sales and use taxes, tax-exempt bond financing, and taxdeductible donations; and
WHEREAS, in order to qualify for property tax exempt status in Cook County, the property utilized by
the non-profit hospital must be exclusively used in a charitable manner, as determined by the Illinois
Department of Revenue during its review of certificates of exemption; and
WHEREAS, currently, the Assessor's Office cannot calculate an approximate assessed value for tax
exempt non-profit hospitals and, therefore, there is no information to gauge the monetary savings nonprofit hospitals accrue through their tax exempt status; and
WHEREAS, unlike a typical homeowner who receives an exemption based on a percentage of the
home's assessed value through the Homeowner's Exemption, a non-profit hospital receives a total
exemption from the hospital's assessed value; and
WHEREAS, in order to fairly and accurately weigh the monetary value of the non-profit hospitals'
property tax exemption against the dollar amount given back to the community through charity care and
other community benefits, it is necessary to analyze the hospital's Community Benefits Plan along with a
report from the Assessor's Office that details each hospital's estimated assessed value and the estimated
exempt dollar amount.

1091

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby require the Cook County Assessor's Office to provide an annual report to the Board listing the
estimated assessed value and the estimated exempt dollar amount of each non-profit hospital in Cook
County beginning with the current year's tri-annual reassessment.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Tax and Revenue Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 270513). The motion carried
unanimously.

HIGHWAY DEPARTMENT MATTERS
NOTICE OF 501 ACCOUNT

Transmitting a Communication, dated March 15, 2005 from
WALLY S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Presented for your information is a list of projects funded from the 501 Illinois First Account that are now
assigned individual section numbers, as required by the Illinois Department of Transportation, to track
Motor Fuel Tax expenditures. The County Board of Commissioners, as part of Cook County's annual
budget, approved the Department of Highway's 501 Account, a Motor Fuel Tax funded account.
Individual appropriations, such as Appropriating or Maintenance Resolutions are not required for these
items by the Illinois Department of Transportation because this account is part of the County's Annual
Budget. The Board will be supplied with continued notification of the advancement of the projects
through established procedures, i.e., permission to advertise, award approval and payment processing as
appropriate.

Services, Inc., Chicago, Illinois.
This maintenance contract consists of furnishing curb lane cleaning services on various sections of the
Cook County Highway system.

on May 4, 2004 in the amount of $397,313.70. A condition of the current contract allows for a one-year
extension at the same terms with mutual written agreement between the parties. Elgin Sweeping
Services, Inc. wishes to extend the existing contract with the Highway Department under the same terms
and conditions for an additional year.

1107

First 501 Account).

104th A venue,
167th Street to 159th Street
in the Village of Orland Park
Section: 05-W2509-04-EG

1116

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

05-R-123
RESOLUTION
APPROPRIATING RESOLUTION
BE IT RESOLVED, by the County Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, that the following
described County Highway be improved under the Illinois Highway Code:

County Highway W25, 104th Avenue, beginning at a point near 167th Street and extending along said
route in a northerly direction to a point near 159th Street, a distance of approximately 1.01 miles; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the appropriation shall be for paying the County's share (75%) of
the costs for a preliminary engineering study, including surveys, soil borings, structural borings and
analyses, drainage investigations, wetlands delineation/classification and geometric investigation and
County reviews in accordance with a subsequent formal agreement with the Village of Orland Park and
shall be designated as Section: 05-W2509-04-EG; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the study shall be conducted by an outside engineering consultant
contracted by the Village of Orland Park; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of Three Hundred Thousand
and No/100 Dollars, ($300,000.00) from the County's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds for the design
of this improvement; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Clerk is hereby directed to transmit two (2) certified copies of
this Resolution to the District Office of the Illinois Department of Transportation.

April 6, 2005

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Appropriating Resolution be
approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 17, 2005 from
WALLY S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Re:

Quick Take Authority
West Bartlett Road,
Spitzer Road to Illinois Route 59
Section: OO-B1003-05-RP

Submitting herewith a Resolution which provides for the acquisition by Quick Take procedures for real
property necessary for the improvement of County Highway B 10, more commonly known as West
Bartlett Road.
This Resolution provides that the Superintendent of Highways of the County of Cook is authorized to
seek Quick Take Authority from the State Legislature pursuant to their procedures. I shall report to the
Cook County Board of Commissioners the results.

1117

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
05-R-124
RESOLUTION
QUICK TAKE AUTHORITY RESOLUTION



WHEREAS, the Highway Department considered the desirability and importance of providing for the
improvement of West Bartlett Road under Section: OO-B1003-05-RP and after such consideration
certified its approval of the proposed improvement to the Cook County Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, the County Board on August 9, 2000 adopted a Resolution providing for the improvement
of West Bartlett Road under Section: OO-B1003-05-RP; and
WHEREAS, having the County Board's approval, the Cook County Superintendent of Highways caused
to be prepared proper surveys, maps, plans, specifications and estimates of cost of the proposed
improvement; and
WHEREAS, said plans and surveys require that private property be taken for such improvement pursuant
to authority granted under the Illinois Highway Code [Chapter 605 of the Illinois Compiled Statutes
(2000), 5/5-801]; and
WHEREAS, the private property to be taken consists of real property legally described in the exhibits
submitted herewith; and
WHEREAS, delay caused by time consuming condemnation litigation to acquire land would result in
increased cost and inconvenience to the public; and
WHEREAS, Quick Take legal procedures will expedite the improvement and result in a scheduled
completion date.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the
Cook County Superintendent of Highways is hereby authorized, empowered and directed on behalf of the
County of Cook to seek Quick Take Authority from the State Legislature pursuant to their procedures for
the West Bartlett Road project.

April 6, 2005
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Quick Take Authority
Resolution be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

and selection of the County Highway has been approved by the Illinois Department of Transportation
("Department"); and
WHEREAS, said County Highway is shown on a map that has been approved by the Department, a copy
of which is on file with the County Clerk of Cook County, Illinois, as well as with the Department, as
provided by statute; and
WHEREAS, the County Board, on September 8, 2004 adopted a Resolution providing for the
improvement of Section: 01-W3019-05-RP of said County Highway; and
WHEREAS, the Resolution has been approved by the Department; and
WHEREAS, the County Board has adopted a Resolution stating that the public interest requires the
improvement of the above mentioned Section of the County Highway and has requested of the
Department that the County Highway be constructed and improved by law; and
WHEREAS, the Department did consider the desirability and importance of the proposed improvement
and determined that the construction will be practically possible; and
WHEREAS, the Department determined that the improvement will be of public utility and convenience
and after such consideration certified its approval of the proposed improvement to the Cook County
Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, having the Department's approval the Cook County Superintendent of Highways caused to
be prepared proper surveys, maps, plans, specifications and estimates of cost of the proposed
improvement; and
WHEREAS, said plans and surveys require that private property be taken for such improvement pursuant
to authority granted under the 605 ILCS (2000) 5/5-801; and
WHEREAS, the private property to be taken consists of real property legally described in the exhibits
submitted herewith.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT, AND IT IS HEREBY RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners that the Cook County Superintendent of Highways is hereby authorized, empowered and
directed on behalf of the County of Cook to negotiate with the owner(s), and/or any parties of interest in
the property described herein, for the purpose of agreeing to the compensation to be paid for the property;
and

1119

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
IT IS HEREBY FURTHER RESOLVED, that in the event the parties cannot agree on the just
compensation to be paid for the taking of the property, the State's Attorney for Cook County, Illinois
shall institute legal proceedings in a court of competent jurisdiction for the purpose of determining the
just compensation to be paid pursuant to the 735 ILCS (2000) 5/7-101. Furthermore, the State's Attorney
is authorized and directed to do any and all acts necessary and proper for the acquisition of the property
described herein.

April 6, 2005
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Right-of-Way Land
Acquisition Resolution be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

1123

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

Reason:

The Guardianship Assistance Desk for minors located on the tenth floor of the Cook County
Administration Building provides assistance to individuals who represent themselves in
obtaining guardianship of minors in the Probate Division of the Circuit Court of Cook
County. Volunteer attorneys counsel clients on guardianship law and help them prepare
necessary court papers with the assistance of court staff. With the assistance of The Chicago
Bar Foundation, the Circuit Court of Cook County has assisted 15,000 pro-se guardianship
litigants over the past ten (10) years.
The Chicago Bar Foundation manages the Guardianship Assistance Desk for minors with the
help of the Chicago Volunteer Legal Services Foundation (CVLS) and court staff. CVLS has
pledged to match the value of the county's contribution to the program.

JUVENILE PROBATION DEPARTMENT
CONTRACT

Transmitting a Communication from
TIMOTHY C. EV ANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Northwestern University,
Evanston, Illinois, to operate the Circuit Court of Cook County's Juvenile Court Clinic.
Reason:

Pursuant to County Contract No. 00-41-1161, Northwestern University has been responsible
since June 2000 for the development, implementation, and staffing of the Juvenile Court
Clinic.
The Juvenile Court Clinic is responsible for providing a variety of services to judges and
court personnel regarding forensic clinical information in juvenile court proceedings. This
information is used by judges, lawyers and probation officers in making informed and
relevant decisions concerning minors and families. Juvenile Court Clinic staff, comprised of
lawyers and mental health professionals who use a multi-disciplinary approach to provide
high quality mental health assessments that are relevant, timely, culturally sensitive, and in a
form that bridges the legal and mental health fields. The clinic was implemented in stages
after an initial pilot period to test the effectiveness of the model and is now operating in all 28
courtrooms of the Juvenile Justice Division and Child Protection Division in Chicago and the
suburban municipal districts.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $1,453,265.00 (Year 2005 - $727,000.00; and Year 2006 - $726,265.00).
Contract period: June 1, 2005 through May 31, 2006. (326-260 Account). Requisition No. 53260008.

PROPOSED HOME INVESTMENT PARTNERSHIPS PROGRAM

Transmitting a Communication, dated March 2, 2005 from
GWENDOLYN D. CLEMONS, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re:

HOME Investment Partnerships Program (HOME Program)

respectfully requesting approval to amend a HOME award granted on April 18, 2000, to allow for the
rehabilitation of a Community Integrated Living Arrangement (CILA) for eight special needs persons on
Owl Drive in Rolling Meadows owned by Clearbrook. The Cook County Board awarded Clearbrook
$600,000.00 for the acquisition of five single-family homes for thirty developmentally disabled persons.
Of the $600,000.00 awarded, Clearbrook has acquired three single-family homes, providing housing for
18 special needs persons. They have expended $360,000.00 from their committed HOME dollars with
$240,000.00 remaining.
Clearbrook desires to rebuild and construct the CILA on Owl Drive because of dangerous Stachbotrys
mold present in the house and is requesting the full amount of $240,000.00 to be used to construct one
home for eight residents. Preliminary construction costs are estimated at $360,000.00. Clearbrook plans
to secure a mortgage with Harris Bank for approximately $120,000.00 in order to fill the gap between
HOME funds and actual construction costs.
Respectfully requesting approval of the amendment of the previously approved use of HOME funds, and
that the Chief Administrative Officer of the County of Cook, or his designee, be authorized to execute on
behalf of the County of Cook any and all documents necessary to further the project approved herein,
including but not limited to subgrantee agreements, intergovernmental agreements, amendments and 
modifications thereto, loan documents, lien assignments, releases of mortgages and liens, and mortgage
assumptions.
Fiscal Impact: None.

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the communication be referred
to the Committee on Business and Economic Development. (Comm. No. 270503). The motion carried
unanimously.
PROPOSED RESOLUTIONS

Transmitting a Communication, dated February 23, 2005 from
GWENDOLYN D. CLEMONS, Director, Department of Planning and Development
submitting the proposed Resolution of the Board of Commissioners, the CEDS report, and the Resolution
of the Cook County Economic Development Advisory Committee for your review, consideration and
approval.
This CEDS report is required by the Economic Development Administration (EDA) of the U.S.
Department of Commerce to entitle Cook County, Chicago and the suburbs to apply for federal EDA
funding for economic development projects. This report must be submitted on an annual basis.

1131

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
Since 2000, EDA has funded over $1.6 million for projects in Chicago and Cook County. These federal
funds have been combined with local match to realize more than $2.8 million of economic development
investment.
Respectfully request the approval of this Honorable Body of the Resolution endorsing the CEDS report.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Resolution of the Board of Cook County Commissioners
Approving the 2003-2004 Comprehensive Economic Development Strategy (CEDS)
WHEREAS, we, the Cook County Board of Commissioners, as the duly elected body governing Cook
County, have received and reviewed the 2003-2004 Comprehensive Economic Development Strategy
(CEDS) and the Resolution of the Cook County Economic Development Advisory Committee; and
WHEREAS, we have found CEDS to fulfill its function to report on the previous year's economic
activities and effectiveness, to identify changes and trends in the region's economic conditions, and to
present the economic development goals and activities for the coming year; and
WHEREAS, CEDS meets the requirements of the Economic Development Administration (EDA) to
qualify Cook County, Chicago and suburban jurisdictions within its boundaries as eligible to apply for
EDA funding of economic development projects.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Cook County Commissioners does
hereby approve this 2003-2004 CEDS for submittal to EDA.

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Business and Economic Development. (Comm. No. 270510). The motion
carried unanimously.

incentive for your consideration.
RSI Investments, LLC requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month abandonment rule under
the Class 6b Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the company can complete its application to
the Assessor of Cook County.
Submitting the company application for Class 6b, the Resolution and report of Elk Grove Village, Illinois,
and a Department of Planning and Development staff report for your information.

1132

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 6b that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for an industrial facility;
and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from RSI
Investment LLC and the Resolution from Elk Grove Village for an abandoned industrial facility located at
1850 Estes Avenue, Elk Grove Village, Cook County, Illinois, Property Index Number 08-35-102-0260000; and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of qualifying
abandonment in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive
months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for 9 months at the time of purchase and that special circumstances are present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners indicate their approval
for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate Classification 6b abatement incentive to the
company for an abandoned industrial facility located at 1850 Estes Avenue, Elk Grove Village, Cook
County, Illinois, under the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Business and Economic Development. (Comm. No. 270511). The motion
carried unanimously.

REAL ESTATE MANAGEMENT DIVISION
REAL ESTATE MATTER
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 21, 2005 from
JOHN W. DAVIS, Director, Real Estate Management Division
requesting approval of the agreement for lease of REDI data to the Woodstock Institute of Chicago. The
Woodstock Institute of Chicago has requested a copy of 2003 Cook County Assessor real estate tax data
computer tapes on property characteristics, commonly known as the County Assessor Property
Characteristics File. The requested information will be used for research purposes whereby Woodstock
Institute of Chicago will attempt to quantify the impact that concentrated foreclosures have on values of
properties in lower income and minority communities and how sub-prime and predatory mortgage
lending in these communities affect community development efforts.

1136

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

The Woodstock Institute of Chicago is a "non-commercial user" within the definition set forth in Cook
County's 05-0-18 (An Amendment to an Ordinance Establishing, and Approving the Increase of, Rental
Charges for the Lease of Cook County Real Estate Tax Data by Commercial Users and Non-Commercial
Users), approved by the Board on March 15, 2005 which governs the leasing and use of certain real estate
tax data. Woodstock Institute of Chicago will pay the County a rental charge of $75.00 for the tax data
tapes, which rental charge is in compliance with the rate schedule prescribed in the Ordinance
Amendment.
Approval recommended.

Commissioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Suffredin, moved that the request of the Director of the
Real Estate Management Division. The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE STATE'S ATTORNEY
GRANT APPLICATION

Transmitting a Communication, dated March 18, 2005 from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney's Office
requesting authorization to apply for a grant in the amount of $73,794.00 from the Illinois Criminal
Justice Information Authority (ICllA) for the State's Attorney's Victim-Offender Conferencing Program
which is part of the State's Attorney's youth diversion crime reduction program known as Project
Reclaim.

1143

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
Through this program, the State's Attorney's Office will contract with an organization that will
coordinate and broaden victim-offender conferencing programs in the Second, Third, Fourth, Fifth and
Sixth Municipal Districts of the Circuit Court of Cook County as well as in the farthest southern Chicago
Police Districts, collectively known as Area 2. Trained community volunteers will bring the victim and
youthful offender face-to-face in a neutral, safe environment, allowing them to work through their dispute
and to create a resolution suitable to all parties. This project will provide a forum for modeling a healthy,
positive and productive form of conflict resolution.
The Jane Addams Juvenile Court Foundation will be contributing the required match for this program.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $73,794.00. Funding period: May 1, 2005 through
December 13, 2005.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Chief of the
Administrative Services Bureau of the State's Attorney's Office be approved. The motion carried
unanimously.

PATRICK M. DURKIN, Boot Camp Director, Sheriff's Impact Incarceration Department
WILLIAM WALLACE, Executive Director, Department of Community Supervision and Intervention
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with ADT Security Services,
Inc. (ADT), Oak Brook, Illinois, for project support to maintain the electronic monitoring equipment used
by the Cook County Sheriff's Office. ADT Security Services, Inc. has been the sole source provider for
this support since the system was purchased from ADT in 1999. Project support includes maintenance of
the host processors and home monitor/receiver units (HMRUS) and transmitters, training of new officers
and the resupply of all consumable items.
Reason:

ADT Security Services, Inc. is the only company in North America that can provide support
for the ELMO-TECH equipment. None of the consumable items are available through
commercial means. Also, no other company in North America distributes the EMS 2000IU
equipment. Therefore, ADT Security Services, Inc. is the only known company that can
provide support.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $365,520.00 [$25,800.00 - (212-449 Account); $24,720.00 - (235-449
Account); and $315,000.00 - (236-449 Account)]. Contract period: March 1, 2005 through February 28,
2006. Requisition Nos. 52120006, 52350010 and 52360010.
The Chief Information Officer has reviewed this item and concurs with this recommendation.
Note: This item also appears under the Sheriff's Department of Community Supervision and Intervention
and the Sheriff's Impact Incarceration Department.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

The Village of Palos Park respectfully requests permission to offer a no cash bid to acquire a Tax

The Village of Palos Park intends to use the parcels as a park or associated recreational uses. The short
term plans are to develop the area as a new green space, including bike paths that will connect with paths
in Palos Heights and eventually Lemont. We have entered into a lease agreement with the Metropolitan
Water Reclamation District for land adjacent to these parcels, which would enhance the land available for
this purpose. The long term goals are to develop a multi-museum exhibition facility to be used by some
or all of the major museums in Chicago. By doing so, the Village of Palos Park believes that this use will
serve as an educational, recreational and cultural facility to serve its own residents, residents of Southwest
Cook County and hopefully beyond.

1.

4.

Photographs of the above-named parcels.

There is no third party requestor involved with this no cash bid.

05-0-21
ORDINANCE

AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE COOK COUNTY ZONING
ORDINANCE REZONING CERTAIN PROPERTY LOCATED
IN LEYDEN TOWNSHIP
WHEREAS, the owner of certain property located in Leyden Township, described in Section 1 herein,
has petitioned the Cook County Board of Commissioners to have the property reclassified from the C-4
General Commercial District to the R-6 General Residence District to rehabilitate an existing apartmenthotel building into a 13 unit apartment building, and a Variation to reduce right interior side yard setback
from 10 feet to 6 feet (existing); reduce rear yard setback from 40 feet to 9 feet (existing); and exceed the
maximum height of principal structure from 2 stories to 2 1/2 to 3 stories (existing, but below the
maximum height of 30 feet); to increase the floor area ratio from .60 to 1.014; to reduce the minimum
size of a dwelling unit from 600 square feet to 500 and 560 square feet for 12 of the 13 units and reduce
the off-street parking spaces from 20 to 18 spaces; and
WHEREAS, the said petition was received by the Zoning Board of Appeals of the County of Cook, as
Dockets #7712 and #77 41 and a public hearing was held in regard to said request, after due notice, all in
accordance with the Cook County Zoning Ordinance and the Statutes of the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the Zoning Board of Appeals entered detailed findings in accordance with the standards set
forth in the Cook County Zoning Ordinance recommending that the Cook County Board of
Commissioners grant said application for Amendment and Variation; and
WHEREAS, it is the opinion of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that said property be
rezoned and reclassified in accordance with the recommendations of the Zoning Board of Appeals.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois:
Section 1: That the following described property be and the same is hereby rezoned from C-4 General
Commercial District to the R-6 General Residence District to rehabilitate an existing
apartment-hotel building into a 13 unit apartment building, and a Variation to reduce right
interior side yard setback from 10 feet to 6 feet (existing); reduce rear yard setback from 40
feet to 9 feet (existing); and exceed the maximum height of principal structure from 2 stories
to 2 1/2 to 3 stories (existing, but below the maximum height of 30 feet); to increase the floor
area ratio from .60 to 1.014; to reduce the minimum size of a dwelling unit from 600 square
feet to 500 and 560 squ~re feet. for 12 of the 13 units and reduce the off-street parking spaces
from 20 to 18 spaces.

JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

1233

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

WHEREAS, County workers care for the ill in our public hospitals and clinics; protect public safety by
plowing roads and policing public lands; ensure the integrity of our criminal justice system through
services that range from legal representation to the maintenance of courthouses; work to expand the
economic vitality of our region through programs that strengthen housing, economic development and
employment; and work with other government agencies, municipalities and private agencies to protect the
quality of our air, water and land; and
WHEREAS, County workers play a vital role as frontline first responders and critical support staff in
local and regional emergencies and as part of the nation's broad commitment to strengthening homeland
security; and
WHEREAS, two-thirds of the public funds expended on Cook County Government go directly to secure
public safety and public health for local residents; and
WHEREAS, other critical services that Cook County provides include job training for displaced workers;
financial incentives to expanding businesses; critical infrastructure improvements, ranging from sewage
systems to fire trucks and public facilities in needy communities; the development of safe, secure,
affordable housing for our seniors throughout Cook County; and single-family home rehabilitation that
helps strengthen and enhance the quality of life for all residents in the region; and
WHEREAS, because of Cook County's employees, County agencies are able to provide efficient, costeffective, responsive public services that enhance the social and economic strengths of our communities;
and
WHEREAS, Cook County employees and agencies provide a range of daily services that are critical to
both the immediate safety and the long-term security of our residents; and
WHEREAS, Cook County Government joins the nation's counties as a critical source of planning and
problem-solving that seeks to strengthen the safety and economic security of our communities; and
WHEREAS, from April 10-16, the National Association of Counties is celebrating National County
Government Week by honoring County 'heroes', employees who work to secure the safety and wellbeing of county residents across the nation.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that I, John H. Stroger, Jr., as President of the Cook County
Board of Commissioners, on behalf of all its residents, do hereby applaud the leadership, innovation and
valuable service provided by the employees of Cook County and all of the nation's counties, and
designate April 10-16, 2005 National County Government Week in honor of County employees,
programs and agencies in Cook County and across the nation; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be promulgated through the
public record.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

WHEREAS, April 9, 2005 marks the
the Bataan Death March; and

~

63rd Anniversary of the Fall of Bataan and the beginning of

WHEREAS, these unspeakably valiant men, both Filipino and American, fought side by side to defend
the sovereign right of freedom; and
WHEREAS, the American Armed Services collaborated extensively, with men hailing from the Army,
Army Air Corps, Navy and Marines to defy the Japanese Invasion; and
WHEREAS, the conditions of battle were harrowing: they fought in a malaria-infested region, surviving
on quarter rations with minimal medical help, and were forced to fight with outdated equipment and
virtually no airpower; and
WHEREAS, 21,000 men died along the 55 mile march to the prisoner-of-war camp, and those who
survived suffered unspeakably at the hands of their Japanese captors; and
WHEREAS, the surviving men of the battle drew from the utmost depth of their spirit to complete the
march during the scorching heat of the jungles.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that I, John H. Stroger, Jr., along with the Cook County
Board of Commissioners, on behalf of the more than five million residents of Cook County, do hereby
offer our most humble thankfulness to the men of the Battle of Bataan.

Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

05-R-130
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN AND JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS AND
BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

WHEREAS, the Tinley Park Mental Health Center ("Tinley Park MHC") in Tinley Park, Illinois
provides a safe and secure treatment setting for mentally ill individuals, including those who have no
insurance or who have exhausted their mental health coverage, for the south suburbs in Cook County, as
well as the City of Chicago; and
WHEREAS, shuttering Tinley Park MHC would dismantle a vital community resource that has taken
decades to develop, providing a well-staffed inpatient treatment center with professional and
paraprofessionals specially trained to serve patients suffering from very severe mental illness as well as
planning which links patients to community outpatient resources; and
WHEREAS, last year, there were more than 2,000 admissions to Tinley Park MHC, a clear indication of
the great need for its services, and the demand for services at the center is increasing with the number of
patients seeking treatment rising by more than 10% over the last two years; and
WHEREAS, there are no comparable alternatives to provide care in the south suburban area and services
at community mental health centers are largely structured to serve individuals who are not in acute crisis
(are not violent, suicidal, or exhibiting extreme behaviors) and without a strong, secure treatment facility,
too many individuals with mental illness are often lost to homelessness, further burdening municipal and
law enforcement authorities; and
WHEREAS, Tinley Park MHC employs more than 300 people in our region, including doctors, nurses
and other professionals and its workers receive fair wages, good benefits and workplace rights; and
WHEREAS, current plans call for stopping Chicago residents from being admitted to Tinley Park MHC
in mid-May; and

1236

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

WHEREAS, Cook County does not have the resources to treat patients denied admission to Tinley Park
MHC; and
WHEREAS, Governor Rod Blagojevich has promised to make increasing health services a state priority.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the County of Cook hereby states its opposition to the
closure of Tinley Park Mental Health Center and urges Governor Blagojevich to reconsider his proposal
to close the facility; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County of Cook urges legislators in the Illinois General
Assembly to adopt a budget that maintains full operation of Tinley Park MHC and protects Cook County
residents; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that suitable copies of this Resolution be delivered to Governor
Blagojevich, Senate President Emil Jones, Jr., House Speaker Michael J. Madigan, and all members of the
Illinois General Assembly who represent Cook County, Illinois; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this Resolution shall take effect on the date of its passage and
approval.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

the General Assembly that effect the services and operation of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the Chairman and Vice Chairman of the Legislation and Intergovernmental Relations
Committee of the Cook County Board have met with the President's Office on the following bills and
have discussed what position the County should take concerning them; and
WHEREAS, there is no opposition to the positions being proposed; and

County Board.

the following bills and encourages their passage: Senate Bills 51, 75, 1443, 1444, 1509~ and House
Bills 350 aaa 2402; and

Constitutional Home Rule powers of Cook County or that imposes an unfunded mandate to spend Cook
County funds; and

Blagojevich, Senate President Emil Jones, Jr., House Speaker Michael J. Madigan, Senator Frank
Watson, Senate Republican Leader, Representative Tom Cross, House Republican Leader and all of Cook
County's duly elected representatives in the General Assembly; and

WHEREAS, Mujeres Latinas en Accion was founded in 1973 and is one of the longest standing Latina
nonprofit organizations in the nation; and
WHEREAS, over the years, Mujeres has developed a comprehensive array of social services and
advocacy initiatives that promote nonviolence and leadership development, offering programs to their
constituency like domestic violence, sexual assault, women in transition, peace program, parent support,
"proyecto juventud", Latina leadership, child care services, sanctuary and mother and daughter programs;
and
WHEREAS, these programs include integrated activities to assist women in exploring choices, make
informed decisions, develop self-esteem, and enhance daily living and problem-solving skills; and
WHEREAS, Mujeres Latinas en Accion, a bilingual/bicultural agency, seeks to empower women, their
families and youth to become self-reliant and be able to take full advantage of available opportunities, and
create new opportunities to improve the quality of their lives; and
WHEREAS, 16 years ago Mujeres Latinas en Accion created the Voces Unidas - Voices United Banquet
to raise funds for basic operations and during these banquets many individuals, women and men and
corporations have been specially recognized for their outstanding service to Chicago's Latinas; and
WHEREAS, Maria Socorro Pesqueira is the President and CEO ofMujeres Latinas en Accion, and under
her leadership Mujeres received the prestigious ORBA Award for Nonprofit Financial Management
Excellence.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, does
hereby honor Mujeres Latinas en Accion for their outstanding service advocating on behalf of Latinas,
improving the quality of life of many families in the Chicago area; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body, and that a suitable copy of same be presented to Maria S. Pesqueria, President and CEO ofMujeres
Latinas en Accion.

WHEREAS, John Edward Grant was the devoted and much beloved father of his daughter, Robyn
Elayne Robinson, her husband, Calvin Lee Robinson and stepson, Dwarrye Grant Collins to whom he
imparted many excellent and stellar qualities; and
WHEREAS, John Edward Grant was the loving brother of William Henry Grant II, Richard Lee Grant
and Laverne Underwood with whom he shared many fine and precious memories; and
WHEREAS, born and raised in Sheffield, Alabama, John Edward Grant graduated as Valedictorian from
Sterling High School and further attained multiple degrees; and
WHEREAS, John Edward Grant honorably served his country in the U. S. Army after which he
completed a thirty-three year career with the U. S. Postal Service; and
WHEREAS, a resident of Chicago since 1973, "Grant" met and married the former State Senator Earlean
Collins, he became one of her strongest advocates for education and services for children and senior
citizens; and
WHEREAS, John Edward Grant used his many gifts in several church ministries while also being
devoted to and active in multiple Chicago-area affiliations, he will be sorely missed by many church
members, colleagues, constituents, and special friends.

County Board of Commissioners, and that a suitable copy of same shall be provided to the family of John

WHEREAS, Ms. Johnson is the co-president of A.P.P.L.E., African-American Parents for Purposeful

WHEREAS, Ms. Johnson has received an award for Outstanding Community Service to Humanity from
Reverend Harrison Bolton, Pastor of the New St. Mary Church, for her unmatched commitment to the

Chicago Business Education Association; and
WHEREAS, as a resident of the South Shore area for over forty years, she takes great pride in her
neighborhood. She works with her neighborhood watch group to prevent crime and drugs from

WHEREAS, for the past 15 years, she has been a member of the Myrtle A. McKenzie Club, dedicated to
supporting social and civic programs for women. She is a proud member of Black on Black Love, an
organization that offers programs and community services that provide positive alternatives to crime. Ms.
Miller is also a mentor for women recently released from prison; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Miller also runs her own shut-in ministry. She provides dinners for friends, neighbors,
and senior citizens when they are sick, and she arranges transportation for them to get to and from
medical appointments. Ms. Miller has been and continues to be devoted to helping others in her
community.

Family Support, director of the Accelerated Academic Achievement Program, and director of Community
Resource Programs; and

Educators, the Chicago Principals and Administrators Association, the Illinois Principals Association, the

four local nursing homes. Also, she participates in the Poppy Days Drive to help raise funds for veterans
in area hospitals; and
WHEREAS, Mrs. O'Leary is an annual participant in the Ton of Food Drive during the Thanksgiving
and Christmas season. She personally crafted and distributed yellow ribbons to the residents of Worth

WHEREAS, it is important to honor all women who have contributed significantly in a wide variety of
ways and touched a number of people with their endeavors; and

WHEREAS, after growing up in the Back of the Yards, and attending St. Augustine High School, Sister
Joellen Tumas joined the religious order of the Poor Handmaids of Jesus Christ, which started her long
career of mission work. From 1966 to 1974, Sister Joellen worked at the Angel Guardian Orphanage on
the north side of Chicago as a teacher and child care worker; and

WHEREAS, when the orphanage closed, she headed back to her alma mater, St. Augustine, to teach 4th
grade and English as a second language for over a decade. To show their appreciation, the students and
faculty of St. Augustine named Sister Joellen alumna of the year in 1992; and

WHEREAS, since 1990, Sister Joellen has been the Pastoral Associate and Food Pantry Director at Holy
Cross/Immaculate Heart of Mary Parish. She has helped the food pantry increase service from 30
families a week in 1990 to 225 families a week currently; and

WHEREAS, Sister Joellen was also able to open the Kids Cafe, which offers hot meals for children ages
2 to 18. Sister Joellen's food pantry has received numerous awards from the Greater Chicago Food
Depository, including Pantry of the Year Award in 2004.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Cook County Board
of Commissioners take this opportunity on behalf of the people of Cook County to express official
personal gratitude and deep appreciation to Sister Joellen Tumas for her outstanding public service and
dedication; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official proceedings
of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, and that a copy thereof be transmitted as a testimonial of
the high esteem and appreciation in which Sister Joellen Tumas is regarded by the Members of the Board
of Commissioners of Cook County.

WHEREAS, the Cook County Commission on Women's Issues created an award to honor those women
who have made exceptional contributions to their communities, families, and professions; and
WHEREAS, it is important to honor all women who have contributed significantly in a wide variety of
ways and touched a number of people with their endeavors; and
WHEREAS, America Sorrentini is regarded as a great humanitarian, organizer, and internationalist in the
greater Humboldt Park area. Ms. Sorrentini was born in Puerto Rico, and realized while pursuing her
education in Mexico that her passion is to organize people to stand up for their rights; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Sorrentini has played a central role in founding numerous human rights organizations
in Chicago, including the Latin United Community Housing Association (LUCHA). LUCHA works to
stabilize the Latino community and other residents of West Town, Humboldt Park, and Logan Square by
developing decent and affordable housing and providing housing services to residents; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Sorrentini has also played a major role in founding other human rights organizations in
Chicago such as the West Town Coalition, Casa Brotherhood of Undocumented Workers, Puerto Rico
Solidarity and Black-Latino Covenance for Harold Washington; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Sorrentini's most recent distinction was her vow to end discrimination by answering
Rosa Park's call to erect a Wall of Tolerance to be unveiled this year at the Civil Rights Center in
Montgomery, Alabama.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Cook County Board
of Commissioners take this opportunity on behalf of the people of Cook County to express official
personal gratitude and deep appreciation to America Sorrentini for her outstanding public service and
dedication; and

1253

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official proceedings
of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, and that a copy thereof be transmitted as a testimonial of
the high esteem and appreciation in which America Sorrentini is regarded by the Members of the Board
of Commissioners of Cook County.

Honoring Charlotte Newfeld, recipient of the

WHEREAS, the Cook County Commission on Women's Issues created an award to honor those women
who have made exceptional contributions to their communities, families, and professions; and

1255

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

WHEREAS, it is important to honor all women who have contributed significantly in a wide variety of
ways and touched a number of people with their endeavors; and
WHEREAS, in 1974, Ms. Newfeld was a founding director of the Friends of the Parks, and in 1975, she
helped to found the Education Resource Center which later evolved into the Children's Museum. She
was a founding member of the District 3 School Council and the founding vice chair of the Walt Disney
Magnet School where she helped to develop the first admission's policy assuring a representative,
integrated school population; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Newfeld has worked in local, state, and national politics as well. She helped in
working with the State Legislature to pass Illinois' first Bilingual Education Act. She has also been a
member of the Independent Voters of Illinois Independent Precinct Organization for over 35 years. She
ran for alderman herself in 1982. One of Ms. Newfeld's most active roles in government was as a
member of the Chicago Commission on Women, where she served from 1984-1990; and
WHEREAS, she was the first woman board member of the Lake View Citizens Council, and she has also
served as president and vice-president. Ms. Newfeld volunteered on behalf of Citizens United for
Baseball in Sunshine (CUBS), the campaign to retain Wrigley Field as the only daytime baseball park in
the Major League. After the introduction of night games, Ms. Newfeld represented the area in designing
and enforcing neighborhood protections; and
WHEREAS, recently, Ms. Newfeld worked to restore the Bill Jarvis Migratory Bird Sanctuary,
supervising 300 volunteers in the effort to revitalize the shelter and feeding site for the millions of
migratory birds that travel the shores of Lake Michigan each year.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Cook County Board
of Commissioners take this opportunity on behalf of the people of Cook County to express official
personal gratitude and deep appreciation to Charlotte Newfeld for her outstanding public service and
dedication; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official proceedings
of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, and that a copy thereof be transmitted as a testimonial of
the high esteem and appreciation in which Charlotte Newfeld is regarded by the Members of the Board of
Commissioners of Cook County.

Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Development Corp. in Wilmette for over a decade. Recently, Ms. Cleland culminated a three-year
advocacy effort when Wilmette passed its first affordable housing plan. Her decades of work to eliminate
housing barriers are helping to improve her community; and
WHEREAS, with her husband, Bob, Ms. Cleland founded SANE/Freeze on the North Shore, a peace
action organization. Ms. Cleland was also a founding member of the North Shore Peace Initiative; and
WHEREAS, she was also involved in social action concerns through First Congregational Church,
U.C.C. in Wilmette from the 1950s to the 1990s.

AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Honoring Norma Morrison, recipient of the
"Unsung Heroine Award", 14th District
WHEREAS, the Cook County Commission on Women's Issues created an award to honor those women
who have made exceptional contributions to their communities, families, and professions; and
WHEREAS, it is important to honor all women who have contributed significantly in a wide variety of
ways and touched a number of people with their endeavors; and
WHEREAS, Norma Morrison, at age 89, remains one of Glenview's most active residents. A crusader
for better government, she serves as a behind-the-scenes editor of the Glenview Watch, an online
community newsletter that covers current events of the village, its park districts, and local schools. She
has been active in the League of Women Voters and serves on Glenview's Historic Preservation
Commission; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Morrison is best known to her community as the woman who saved Wagner Farm, the
last working farm in Chicago's near suburbs. She formed the Citizens Organized for Wagner's, better
known as COWS, to petition, speak and march for the farm. The COWS were successful; the farm is now
owned by Glenview's Park District and will serve as an educational and recreational center for the
community; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Morrison's earlier battles included an effort in the mid 1950s to close the Lutter Dump,
an uncontrolled, unsanitary landfill causing immense amounts of pollution in residential areas of
Glenview. Ms. Morrison rallied the support of young mothers and children in the area. This mothers'
crusade against the dump proved successful; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Morrison ran for the village board, and in 1957, became the first woman ever elected to
public office in Glenview.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Cook County Board
of Commissioner take this opportunity on behalf of the people of Cook County to express official
congratulations, personal gratitude and appreciation to Norma Morrison for her outstanding service and
dedication; and

1261

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official proceedings
of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, and that a copy thereof be transmitted as a testimonial of
the high esteem in which Norma Morrison is regarded by the Members of the Board of Commissioners of
Cook County and its residents.

Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
HONORING DANIEL D. SCANLON
WHEREAS, Daniel D. Scanlon will end his term as Mayor of Morton Grove on April 11, 2005 and retire
after a lifetime of public service; and
WHEREAS, Daniel D. Scanlon served in the 84th Infantry Division in World War II and fought in the
Battle of the Bulge; and
WHEREAS, Mayor Scanlon dedicated more than 35 years of public service to the Village of Morton
Grove including working as the Village electrical inspector, serving as a Morton Grove Trustee for eight
years and serving as Mayor from 1996 to 2005; and

1266

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

WHEREAS, under Mayor Scanlon's leadership, the Village made major investments in the community's
infrastructure including virtually reconstructing the entire water utility, remodeling the fire stations,
improving or reconstructing streets, initiating alley improvements, and creating a neighborhood street
lighting program; and
WHEREAS, Mayor Scanlon helped guide the reorganization of the Village staff to maximize
professionalism, efficiency, and cost-effectiveness; and
WHEREAS, during Mayor Scanlon's first term, the Village seamlessly transitioned to a new starting
date for its fiscal year, now beginning on January 1 to better synchronize with the private sector and
Illinois tax cycles; and
WHEREAS, under Mayor Scanlon's leadership, the Village significantly improved its fiscal operations
and implemented procedures to make the budget process easier for staff and residents which has resulted
in a number of CAFR awards for the Village; and
WHEREAS, one of Mayor Scanlon's priorities was expanding economic development in the Village; he
oversaw the creation of two TIF Districts, helped attract a number of new retail stores and two car
dealerships, worked with property owners to remodel the Harlem-Dempster Plaza, and redeveloped the
Lehigh-Ferris TIF into a thriving residential neighborhood; and
WHEREAS, Mayor Scanlon was a dedicated public servant who worked diligently with elected officials,
governmental agencies, businesses, and civic organizations at the local and state levels; and
WHEREAS, Mayor Scanlon's proudest accomplishment was the Village's purchase of the American
Legion Memorial Civic Center and the completion of its remodeling which resulted in the Civic Center
becoming the premier community meeting place and a centralized site for social services and
governmental meetings; and
WHEREAS, Mayor Scanlon was also active in the c1v1c life of Morton Grove; he worked as a
fundraising volunteer for the Muscular Dystrophy Association of Illinois, held membership in the IBEW
Local #134 for over 50 years, was a founding member of Morton Grove American Legion Post #134, and
still attends St. Martha's Parish; and
WHEREAS, throughout his career as an elected official, Daniel D. Scanlon always prioritized the
Village of Morton Grove and worked tirelessly to improve the community for the benefit of all residents.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby thank Daniel D. Scanlon for his service as an elected official and Mayor of the Village of Morton
Grove and commends him for his hard work on behalf of the citizens of Morton Grove; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Daniel D.
Scanlon as a symbol of this auspicious occasion and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings of
this Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

1267

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, Peter Moy has dedicated more than 10 years of public service to the Village of
Lincolnwood including serving as a Lincolnwood Trustee for four years and as Village President from
2001 to 2005; and
WHEREAS, under President Moy's leadership, the Village completed the construction of several major
projects including the Connector Road in the Northeast Parkway Industrial District, the new public
aquatic center, and the Touhy/Crawford public parking lot; and
WHEREAS, during President Moy's term, the Village maintained a high bond rating; and
WHEREAS, one of President Moy's priorities was promoting economic development in the Village; his
efforts helped the Village increase its sales tax revenue by $1.2 million dollars between 2001 and 2005
with the addition of several new retail stores; and
WHEREAS, to help encourage property improvements across the Village, President Moy implemented
the Property Enhancement Program and the Parkway Enhancement Grant Program for businesses; and
WHEREAS, President Moy recognized the importance of protecting the integrity and character of the
Village's residential neighborhoods; he was instrumental in the adoption of the Landscape Ordinance and
in the adoption of new regulations pertaining to the construction of new single family homes; and
WHEREAS, President Moy oversaw the formation of the Lincoln Avenue Task Force and the Traffic
Commission; and
WHEREAS, President Moy was a member of the Board of Trustees for the Solid Waste Agency of
Northern Cook County and the Northwest Municipal Conference; and
WHEREAS, President Moy directly supported community agencies through his participation as a Board
Member of the United Way and the Lincolnwood School Foundation; and
WHEREAS, for his dedication to the Village of Lincolnwood, President Moy was the 2002 recipient of
the Federation of Mid-American Chinese Academic Organizations Award; and
WHEREAS, President Moy was a dedicated public servant who worked diligently with elected officials,
governmental agencies, businesses, and civic organizations at the local and state levels; and
WHEREAS, throughout his career as an elected official, Peter Moy always prioritized the Village of
Lincolnwood and worked tirelessly to improve the community for the benefit of all residents.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby thank Peter Moy for his service as an elected official and President of the Village of Lincolnwood
and commends him for his hard work on behalf of the citizens of Lincolnwood; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Peter Moy as a
symbol of this auspicious occasion and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst Edward J. Moskal; and

1272

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

WHEREAS, Edward J. Moskal, president of the Polish National Alliance (PNA) and the Polish
American Congress (PAC), passed away at his home in the Edgebrook neighborhood of Chicago on
March 22, 2005; and
WHEREAS, under his nearly two-decades of leadership, the Polish National Alliance implemented its
own banking institution, radio station and technology-friendly infrastructure. With a membership of
250,000, the PNA is the largest ethnic fraternal organization in the United States; and
WHEREAS, Edward Moskal had also served as president of the Polish American Congress since 1988.
The PAC is an umbrella organization of 1,200 Polish-American fraternal, veteran and cultural groups; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Moskal was passionate in his dedication to Polish-American citizens, preserving the
Polish culture and tradition in the United States, and to the people of Poland. He made several
humanitarian-related trips to Poland and accompanied former Vice-President Al Gore to the Ghetto
Uprising anniversary ceremony in Warsaw; and
WHEREAS, his numerous achievements on behalf of Polish people worldwide earned him Poland's
highest civilian honor, an honorary citizenship of Krakow and an honorary doctorate from the University
of Poznan Medical School; and
WHEREAS, Edward Moskal will be remembered by countless people, including world leaders and
government officials throughout Illinois and the United States, as an outspoken, tireless advocate of the
Polish people and their heritage; and
WHEREAS, Edward J. Moskal will be deeply missed by his wife, Wanda; daughter, Pamela; sister,
Irene; brother, Chester; and grandchildren and great-grandchildren.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Board of Commissioners of Cook
County do hereby express their heartfelt sympathies to the family of Edward J. Moskal and the PolishAmerican citizens of Cook County and hope they find comfort in the inspirational legacy he leaves
behind; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be prepared for the Moskal
family that his memory may be so honored.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

organization in the United States and its purpose is to promote the Italian culture, foster camaraderie,
provide financial security through life insurance and combat prejudice and discrimination; and
WHEREAS, on Saturday, April 23, 2005, the IANU will hold its annual Michelangelo Awards banquet
and will honor Anthony Lupo with this award; and
WHEREAS, Anthony Lupo, a resident and successful businessman in Norridge, Illinois, is the co-owner
of Cumberland Funeral Chapels and has been a funeral director for 35 years. He is well-known for his
compassion and efficiency in dealing with clients at their most stressful and painful moments; and
WHEREAS, in addition to operating a demanding business, Anthony Lupo dedicates his scarce free time
to many organizations that enhance the quality of life for Italian Americans. He has been a member of the
IANU for 25 years, initially with the Paterno Lodge. Over 20 years ago, he founded the St. Anthony
Lodge and continues to serve on its board. Mr. Lupo is also a member of UNICO, an Italian-American
organization that raises funds for several Italian charities, and a member of Boys Town of Italy, an
American-founded charity for Italian youth; and
WHEREAS, Anthony Lupo is a devoted husband to Stephanie, loving father to Domenica and Anthony,
Jr., dear friend to countless people and respected businessman and community leader.

AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Richard E. Stamz was born April 10, 1906 in Memphis, Tennessee, graduating from
Lemoyne High School and attended Lemoyne Owens College before moving to Chicago in 1936; and
WHEREAS, Richard Stamz began his life in Chicago working as a busboy at the Edgewater Beach Hotel
where Ann Sothern recognized his talents. Stamz went on the tour with Ms. Sothem and her band which
introduced him to show business; and
WHEREAS, Richard Stamz began his legendary career in radio during the late 1940s with his acclaimed
radio program "Open the Door Richard" and debuted his "Richard's Open Door" television program in
January 1956; and
WHEREAS, Richard Stamz's popularity as a radio and television personality spread throughout the
country and earned him the name "Crown Prince of Disc Jockeys"; and

1276

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

WHEREAS, the pioneering efforts of Richard Stamz opened the doors of opportunity for Blacks in radio
and television; and
WHEREAS, Richard Stamz was instrumental in organizing black radio and television stars in 1952
resulting in the formation of the National Association of Television and Radio Announcers (NATRA)
serving as chairman until 1961; and
WHEREAS, Richard E. Stamz worked as a community and political activist throughout his life to
improve the quality of life for Chicago's Black community and has received numerous professional, civic,
and community awards and honors reflecting his commitment; and
WHEREAS, the Members of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County are proud to recognize
significant events in the lives of its citizens.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby congratulate Richard E. Stamz on his 99th birthday; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be placed in the official proceedings of
this Honorable Body and a suitable copy of same be prepared and presented to Richard Stamz.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
