Congratulating William P. Siffermann on his Retirement from Cook County
WHEREAS, William P. Siffermann worked for Cook County Juvenile Probation and Court Services for
34 years and his last day at the office was March 24, 2005; and

1277

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
WHEREAS, throughout his career with Cook County, Bill Siffermann was an outstanding employee
whose professionalism and leadership lead to his rise through the ranks of Juvenile Probation from his
starting position as a probation officer to the position of Deputy Director which he assumed in 1995; and
WHEREAS, as Deputy Director, Bill Sifferman served as Chief Deputy Administrator for a department
comprised of 550 employees with an annual budget of more than $40 million; and
WHEREAS, as manager and supervisor, Bill Siffermann prioritized sharing his knowledge and
experience with his co-workers and made himself available to all staff; he was responsible for developing
and implementing departmental policies and providing staff with operational guidelines and standards of
performance; and
WHEREAS, Bill Siffermann was instrumental in developing, implementing, and helping to secure
funding for programs related to public safety including the Intensive Probation Program, Intensive Drug
Program, Home Confinement Program, Detention Screening, Evening Reporting Centers, Electronic
Monitoring Program and the nationally recognized Cook County Juvenile Detention Alternatives
Initiative; and
WHEREAS, Bill Siffermann recognized the importance of collaborative working relationships and
regularly participated in planning sessions with the Presiding Judges of Juvenile Justice and Child
Protection Divisions as well as other juvenile justice agencies; and
WHEREAS, Bill Siffermann's expertise was recognized by juvenile justice professionals across the
nation; he was a national presenter on juvenile justice administration and detention reform for many
agencies including the National Association of Juvenile and Family Court Judges, National Juvenile
Detention Association, Annie E. Casey Foundation National Detention Conferences and the Chicago
Police Department; and
WHEREAS, Bill Siffermann was dedicated to his job working to help troubled youth turn their lives
around and promoting and ensuring public safety.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby thank William P. Siffermann for his years of service to Cook County and wishes him success in
his future endeavors in San Francisco; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to William P.
Siffermann as a symbol of this auspicious occasion and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings
of this Honorable Body.

JOHN P. DALEY, Chairman, Committee on Finance
Your Committee on Finance has considered and reviewed the subject of the Annual Levy of Taxes for the
Fiscal Year A.D., 2005, together with the several sums necessary to be levied to meet the needs and
requirements of the County of Cook for that period.
The Committee, therefore, requests your careful consideration and examination of the "Resolution for the
Levy of Taxes for the Fiscal Year A.D., 2005," submitted herewith, and further recommends its adoption
and passage by the Board of Commissioners.

05-R-163
RESOLUTION
FOR THE LEVY OF TAXES FOR THE FISCAL YEAR 2005
WHEREAS, the Committee on Finance of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, has
considered the subject of the Annual Tax Levy for the Fiscal Year A.D., 2005, and the several sums
necessary to be levied to meet the needs and requirements of the County of Cook for said fiscal year, and
has recommended that this Resolution for the Levy of Taxes be adopted; and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, approved, passed, and adopted the
Annual Appropriation Bill of the County of Cook, for its Fiscal Year 2005, and which said Appropriation
Bill is hereinafter set forth, together with an additional marginal column therein captioned: "AMOUNTS
OF APPROPRIATIONS PAY ABLE FROM THE TAX LEVY".
THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED AND ORDERED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, that the sum of $720,483,542 which is to be collected from the
Annual Tax Levy for the Fiscal Year A.D., 2005 of the County of Cook for the Corporate Fund purposes
of said County, and for the Public Safety Fund purposes of said County, and for the Health Program Fund
purposes of said County, and for the payment of principal and interest on general obligation bonds of said
County, and for Cook County Employees Annuity and Benefit Fund, and for the Election Fund: said sum
being the total amount of appropriations heretofore legally made and contained in the Annual
Appropriation Bill (hereinafter set forth in the Resolution) for the Fiscal Year 2005 duly adopted by the
Board of Commissioners of Cook County, on Thursday, February 24, 2005, at a meeting convened on
January 5, 2005 and concluded on February 24, 2005 be and said sum of $720,483,542 is hereby levied
on and upon all taxable property in the said County of Cook for the current Fiscal Year 2005. The
specific amounts herein levied for the various purposes heretofore named are stated in this Resolution,
and Tax Levy, by being listed and itemized in the separate columns captioned: "AMOUNTS OF
APPROPRIATION PAYABLE FROM THE TAX LEVY". The tax hereby levied for said Fiscal Year
2005 for said appropriations, to be collected from this Levy, being the aforesaid total, consists of the
following specific amount levied for the various purposes hereinafter set forth:

The motion to approve CARRIED.

05-R-164
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the federal government continues to look for ways to contain costs as the national debt
rises; and
WHEREAS, the President drafted a budget for Federal Fiscal Year 2006 that proposed to cut Medicaid
by $65 billion; and
WHEREAS, the President's budget seeks to cut Medicaid through severely limiting or eliminating the
ways in which local governments can assist states in drawing on federal dollars to support the growing
and uninsured populations; and
WHEREAS, since the inception of the Medicaid program, federal law has permitted states to use local
finds as part of the required non-federal share of Medicaid funding; and

1282

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

WHEREAS, the Cook County Bureau of Health Services provides access to a full continuum of
comprehensive health services for the medically underserved; and
WHEREAS, safety net hospitals, including those of the Cook County Bureau of Health Services, and
private hospitals with high numbers of Medicaid patients rely heavily on the dollars generated to the State
of Illinois and to Cook County, through an intergovernmental transfer, a legitimate way in which the State
and Cook County have substantially funded the Medicaid program for almost fifteen years; and
WHEREAS, the Administration's budget proposal calls for reductions in the program to be made
through the limitation or elimination of intergovernmental transfers; and
WHEREAS, Cook County and its Bureau of Health Services Stroger Hospital of Cook County continue
to be legally responsible for the growing uninsured, underinsured, Medicaid and the generally
underserved populations within the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, these safety net facilities would be unfairly affected by the federally proposed cutbacks.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that President John H. Stroger, Jr., and the Cook County
Board of Commissioners commend and support Congress in its recent vote in the United States Senate, to
strike proposed budget cuts from the Senate Budget Resolution and the establishment of a Medicaid
Commission that will review the overall program and make recommendations to the Administration and
Congress for reform; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that we further call on members of the Illinois delegation, Congress
and the Administration, that as they undertake this next process to review Medicaid, that they work jointly
with Cook County and the other local governments and safety net providers to develop and recommend
needed changes; such changes must take into account the strong need to protect safety net hospitals, who,
not only serve the underserved and indigent, but who provide services that we all rely on trauma care,
emergency care, neo-natal care and other specialty children's services and burn services to name a few.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005 .
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

1283

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005

* * * * *
05-R-165
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called Pope John Paul II from our midst; and
WHEREAS, even in the face of profound physical challenges such as a vicious gunshot wound,
Parkinson's disease and advanced age, the Pope's faith never wavered and he quickly became the
embodiment of dignity, courage and unrelenting faith; and
WHEREAS, as a man who was himself very familiar with the pain of oppressive communist rule, people
around the world were moved by the Pope's conviction relative to the concepts of freedom and justice
when, on Christmas eve in 1981, he lit a single candle in the window of his Vatican residence in a
showing of solidarity with suffering nations around the globe; and
WHEREAS, internationally-admired for his unending compassion and unwavering faith, the pope
demonstrated each day that, regardless of one's position in life, in the end, we all answer to God; and
WHEREAS, with Cook County having one of the largest Polish populations outside of Warsaw, Poland,
many from our Polish communities can vividly remember how they were captivated and spiritually
moved by the Pope's 1979 visit to Chicago; and
WHEREAS, with the passing of Pope John Paul II, we have lost a courageous man who overcame the
shackles of oppression to become a revered champion of fairness, freedom and the eradication of
discrimination.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf
of the more than five million residents of Cook County, and countless mourners around the world, does
hereby express its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy on the passing of our beloved
religious leader, Pope John Paul II; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be promulgated through the
public record so that the rich legacy of Pope John Paul II may be so honored and ever cherished.

1284

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 6, 2005
Approved and adopted this 6th day of April 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

and adopted. President Stroger called for a rising vote. The motion carried unanimously.
